No suit, prosecution or other legal proceeding whatsoever shall lie against any person for or in respect of anything which is in good faith done or intended to be done under this Ordinance.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">_________________________________________________</p><p style="text-align: justify;">1 Throughout this Ordinance, the words “Bangladesh” and “Government” were substituted for the words “Pakistan” and “Provincial Government” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">2 Sub-section (1A) was inserted by the Collective Fines (Second Amendment) Ordinance, 1942 (Ordinance No. XLIX of 1942)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">3 Sub-section (3A) was inserted by the Collective Fines (Second Amendment) Ordinance, 1942 (Ordinance No. XLIX of 1942)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Throughout this Ordinance, the words “Bangladesh” and “Government” were substituted for the words “Pakistan” and “Provincial Government” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision and Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Source : Ministry of Law, Justice and Parliamentary Affairs</p>                       </div></div>
155	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">THE COMMERCIAL DOCUMENTS EVIDENCE ACT, 1939 </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p align="center"><strong>THE COMMERCIAL DOCUMENTS EVIDENCE ACT, 1939</strong></p><p align="center">(ACT NO. XXX OF 1939)</p><p align="right">[26th September, 1939]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">An Act to amend the Law of Evidence with respect to certain commercial documents. 1</p><p style="text-align: justify;">WHEREAS it is expedient to amend the Law of Evidence with respect to certain commercial documents;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">It is hereby enacted as follows:-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Short title and extent </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1. (1) This Act may be called the Commercial Documents Evidence Act, 1939.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) It extends to the whole of Bangladesh.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Statements of relevant facts in scheduled documents to be themselves relevant facts</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">2. Notwithstanding anything contained in the Evidence Act, 1872, statements of facts in issue or of relevant facts made in any document included in the Schedule as to matters usually stated in such document shall be themselves relevant facts within the meaning of that Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Presumption as to genuineness of documents</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">3. For the purposes of the Evidence Act, 1872, and notwithstanding anything contained therein, a Court-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        shall presume, within the meaning of that Act, in relation to documents included in Part I of the Schedule, and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        may presume, within the meaning of that Act, in relation to documents included in Part II of the Schedule-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">that any document purporting to be a document included in Part I or Part II of the Schedule, as the case may be, and to have been duly made by or under the appropriate authority, was so made and that the statements contained therein are accurate.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Definition </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">4. In the Schedule the expression “recognised Chamber of Commerce” means a Chamber of Commerce recognised by the Government of its country as being competent to issue certificates of origin, and includes any other association similarly recognised.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">__________________________________________________</p><p style="text-align: justify;">1 Throughout this Act, the word “Bangladesh” was substituted for the word “Pakistan” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Source : Ministry of Law, Justice and Parliamentary Affairs</p>                       </div></div>
156	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">THE CRIMINAL LAW AMENDMENT ACT, 1938 </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p align="center"><strong>THE CRIMINAL LAW AMENDMENT ACT, 1938</strong></p><p align="center">(ACT NO. XX OF 1938)</p><p align="right">[14th September, 1938]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">An Act to amend the criminal law. 1</p><p style="text-align: justify;">WHEREAS it is expedient to supplement the criminal law by providing for the punishment of certain acts prejudicial to the recruitment of persons to serve in, and to the discipline of, the Armed Forces of Bangladesh;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">It is hereby enacted as follows:-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Short title, extent and commencement</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1. (1) This Act may be called the Criminal Law Amendment Act, 1938.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) It extends to the whole of Bangladesh.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) It shall come into force on such date as the Government may, by notification in the official Gazette, appoint in this behalf, 2[ * * *]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Dissuasion from enlistment and instigation to mutiny or insubordination after enlistment</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">2. Whoever-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        with intent to affect adversely the recruitment of persons to serve in the Military, Naval or Air Forces of 3[ Bangladesh], wilfully dissuades or attempts to dissuade the public or any person from entering any such Forces, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        without dissuading or attempting to dissuade any person from entering such Forces, instigates the public or any person to do, after entering any such Force, anything which is an offence punishable as mutiny or insubordination 4[ 31 of the Army Act, 1952, or sections 36, 40 and 41 of the Navy Ordinance, 1961, or sections 37 and 42 of the Air Force Act, 1953], as the case may be,</p><p style="text-align: justify;">shall be punishable with imprisonment for a term which may extend to one year, or with fine, or with both.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">No person shall be prosecuted for any offence under this Act except with the previous sanction of the Government.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Exception 1.- The provisions of clause (a) of this section do not extend to comments on or criticism of the policy of Government in connection with the Military, Naval or Air Forces, made in good faith without any intention of dissuading from enlistment.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Exception 2.- The provisions of clause (a) of this section do not extend to the case in which advice is given in good faith for the benefit of the individual to whom it is given, or for the benefit of any member of his family or of any of his dependants.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">___________________________________________</p><p style="text-align: justify;">1 Throughout this Act, the words “Bangladesh” and “Government” were substituted for the words “Pakistan” and “Provincial Government” respectively by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">2 The words “for the territories under its administration” were omitted by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">3 The word “Bangladesh” was substituted for the words “His Majesty” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision and Declaration) 9Amendment) Act, 1974 (Act No. LIII of 1974)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">4 The figure, words and commas “31 of the Army Act, 1952, or sections 36, 40 and 41 of the Navy Ordinance, 1961, or sections 37 and 42 of the Air Force Act, 1953” were substituted for the figures, words and commas “31 of the Pakistan Army Act, 1952 or sections 10 to 12 and 14 to 17 inclusive of the Naval Discipline Act as applied to the Pakistan Navy by the Pakistan Navy (Discipline) Act, 1934, or section 37 and 42 of the Pakistan Air Force Act, 1953,”, by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Source : Ministry of Law, Justice and Parliamentary Affairs</p>                       </div></div>
157	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">THE CRIMINAL LAW (INDUSTRIAL AREAS) AMENDMENT ACT, 1942 </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p align="center"><strong>THE CRIMINAL LAW (INDUSTRIAL AREAS) AMENDMENT ACT, 1942</strong></p><p align="center">(BENGAL ACT NO. IV OF 1942)</p><p align="right">[4th June, 1942]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">An Act to prevent theft of unidentifiable articles in industrial areas.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">WHEREAS it is expedient to prevent theft of unidentifiable articles in industrial areas;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">It is hereby enacted as follows:-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Short title and extent </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1. (1) This Act may be called the 2[ * * *] Criminal Law (Industrial Areas) Amendment Act, 1942.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) This section and section 2 extend to the whole of 3[ Bangladesh], except the district of Sylhet and the remaining provisions of this Act shall extend to any area declared to be an industrial area under section 2.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Declaration of industrial area </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">2.         The 4[ * * *] Government may, by notification in the official Gazette, declare any area to be an industrial area for the purposes of this Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Apprehension and punishment of persons armed or previously convicted of theft or of other persons</p><p style="text-align: justify;">3.         Any person found, between sunset and sunrise-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        armed with any dangerous or offensive instrument whatsoever, with intent to commit any criminal act;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) disguised in any manner with intent to commit any criminal act;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c)        in any dwelling house or other building whatsoever, without being able satisfactorily to account for his presence therein; or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">any person previously convicted of theft found between sunset and sunrise on board any vessel or boat, or lying or loitering in any bazar, street, yard, thoroughfare or other place who shall not give any satisfactory account of himself; or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">any person having in his possession, without lawful excuse (the proof of which excuse shall be on such person) any instrument of house-breaking;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">may be taken into custody by any police-officer without a warrant, and shall be liable, on summary conviction before a Magistrate, to imprisonment, for a term which may extend to three months.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Explanation.- In this section the word “street” means any road, lane, footway, square, court, alley or passage, whether a thoroughfare or not, to which the public have, permanently or temporarily, a right of access.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Possession or dealing with thing stolen or fraudulently obtained</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">4. (1) Whoever has in his possession, or conveys in any manner, or offers for sale or pawn, anything which there is reason to believe to have been stolen or fraudulently obtained shall, if he fails to account for such possession or such act to the satisfaction of the Magistrate, be liable to fine which may extend to one hundred Taka, or to imprisonment, for a term which may extend to six months.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) If any person charged under sub-section (1) in respect of anything declares that he received such thing from some person, or that he was employed as a carrier, agent or servant to convey such thing for some other person, the Magistrate, after such further inquiry (if any) as he may deem necessary, may summon such other person, and any former or pretended purchaser or other person through whose possession such thing is alleged to have passed, to appear before him, and may examine such person and any witnesses who are produced to testify to such receipt, employment or possession; and, if it appears to such Magistrate that any such person had possession of such thing and had reasonable cause to believe that it was stolen or fraudulently obtained, the Magistrate may punish him with fine which may extend to one hundred Taka, or with imprisonment, for a term which may extend to six months.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">____________________________________________________</p><p style="text-align: justify;">1 Throughout this Act, the word “Taka” was substituted for the word “rupees” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">2 The word “Bengal” was omitted by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">3 The word “Bangladesh” was substituted for the words “East Pakistan” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">4 The word “Provincial” was omitted by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Source : Ministry of Law, Justice and Parliamentary Affairs</p>                       </div></div>
158	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">  THE CUTCHI MEMONS ACT, 1938   </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p align="center"><strong>THE CUTCHI MEMONS ACT, 1938</strong></p><p align="center">(ACT NO. X OF 1938)</p><p align="right">[8th April, 1938]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">An Act to provide that all Cutchi Memons shall be governed in matters of succession and inheritance by the 1[ Muslim] Law.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">WHEREAS it is expedient that all Cutchi Memons be governed in matters of succession and inheritance by the 2[ Muslim] Law;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">It is hereby enacted as follows:-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Short title and commencement</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1. (1) This Act may be called the Cutchi Memons Act, 1938.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) It shall come into force on the 1st day of November, 1938.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Cutchi Memons to be governed in certain matter by Muslim Law</p><p style="text-align: justify;">2. Subject to the provisions of section 3, all Cutchi Memons shall, in matters of succession and inheritance, be governed by the 3[ Muslim] Law.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Savings</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">3. Nothing in this Act shall affect any right or liability acquired or incurred before its commencement, or any legal proceeding or remedy in respect of any such right or liability; and any such legal proceeding or remedy may be continued or enforced as if this Act had not been passed.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">_____________________________________</p><p style="text-align: justify;">1 The word “Muslim” was substituted for the word “Muhammadan” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">2 The word “Muslim” was substituted for the word “Muhammadan” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">3 The word “Muslim” was substituted for the word “Muhammadan” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Source : Ministry of Law, Justice and Parliamentary Affairs</p>                       </div></div>
159	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">THE DEVELOPMENT ACT, 1935 </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p align="center"><strong>THE DEVELOPMENT ACT, 1935</strong></p><p align="center">(ACT NO. XVI OF 1935)</p><p align="right">[3rd October, 1935]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">An Act to provide for the development of lands in Bangladesh and to impose a levy in respect of increased profit resulting from improvement works constructed by the Government.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">WHEREAS it is expedient to provide for the development of lands in Bangladesh and for that purpose to impose a levy in respect of increased profits resulting from improvement works constructed by the Government and to provide further powers in regards to works of improvement;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">2[ * * *]It is hereby enacted as follows:-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Short title, extent and commencement</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1. (1) This Act may be called the 3[ * * *] Development Act, 1935.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) It extends to the whole of Bangladesh.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) It shall come into force on such date as the Government may, by notification, appoint.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Definitions </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">2. In this Act, unless there is anything repugnant in the subject or context,-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(1)        ''agricultural lands'' include lands used for the growing of vegetables and the like but does not include fruit gardens, orchards or homestead lands;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2)        ''canal'' means a canal as defined in clause (1)of section 3 of the Irrigation Act, 1876.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3)        "Collector" includes any officer specially appointed by the Government to perform all or any of the functions of a Collector under this Act;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(4)        "dead or decayed river" includes any river into which, or along any part of which, water has ceased to flow as freely as it would have flowed if it had not been diverted or obstructed whether owing to natural causes or as a result of interference by man, and includes also any depression which at one time formed part of a riverbed but through which there is no longer any perennial flow of water;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(5)        "improvement work'' means any work of improvement constructed before 4[ the 26th day of March, 1971,] by the Government or constructed or proposed to be constructed after that date by the Government which the Government has, by notification, declared to be an improvement work for the purposes of this Act;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(6)        ''notification'' means a notification published in the official Gazette.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(7)        "notified area" means any area in respect of which the Government has, by a notification issued under sub-section (1) of section 5, declared its intention to impose an improvement levy, and includes any part of such area;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(8)        ''period of objection'' means a period mentioned in a notification under this Act within which objections or suggestions will be received;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(9)        ''prescribed'' means prescribed by rules made under this Act; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(10)      ''rent'' and ''tenant'' have the same meanings as in the</p><p style="text-align: justify;">5[ * * *] State Acquisition and Tenancy Act, 1950.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Preliminary notification of intention to impose improvement levy</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">3. Whenever, in the opinion of the Government, any improvement work has increased or is likely to increase the profits from the produce from any agricultural land, or to increase the outturn of such produce, within any area, the Government may, by notification, declare its intention to impose an improvement levy within that area.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Publication of particulars</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">4. A notification under section 3 shall state the following particulars-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) as full a description of the improvement work as, in the opinion of the Government may be practicable;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) the object for which such work has been, or is proposed to be, constructed; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c) the boundaries of the area within which the Government intends to impose the improvement levy.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Abandonment of intention or declaration of intention to impose improvement levy</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">5. (1) After the expiry of a period for objection to be mentioned in a notification under section 3 the Government shall consider the objections and suggestions, if any, receive by it and thereafter shall, by notification, declare its intention either wholly to refrain from imposing the improvement levy or to impose the same in the area concerned or in a specified part thereof, whereupon the area in respect of which the Government has by such a notification declared its intention to impose the improvement levy shall be deemed for the purposes of this Act, to be a notified area.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The Government may, so far as may be in the manner hereinbefore provided, from time to time include in or exclude from any notified area any area which, in the opinion of the Government has benefited or has not benefited, as the case may be, from the improvement work.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">[Omitted]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">6.         [Omitted by the First Schedule of the East Pakistan Repealing and Amending Ordinance, 1962 (Ordinance No. XIII of 1962).]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Imposition of Improvement levy</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">7. When the Government is satisfied that a notified area has benefited or is likely to benefit from an improvement work, if may, by notification, subject to the provisions of section 6, impose improvement levy in that area from such date as may be specified in the notification.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Estimate of increased outturn of produce from agricultural land</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">8. (1) From time to time an officer appointed by the Government shall, in accordance with rules made under this Act, and after hearing any objections in the prescribed manner, prepare in respect of land throughout a notified area an estimate of the average increase in the outturn of the produce from agricultural land of any class which, in his opinion, has been or is likely to be made possible by any improvement work 6[ * * *]:</p><p style="text-align: justify;">7[ * * *]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The 8[ Government] shall, by notification, publish such estimate and, after a period for objection to be specified in such notification, shall consider the objections and suggestions, if any, received by it 9[ * * *]. Thereafter the Government may reject the estimate or may, by notification, accept it with or without modification, whereupon the accuracy of any estimate so accepted shall not be questioned in any court.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) Where an estimate has been accepted under sub-section (2) in respect of a notified area before the imposition of the improvement levy, such estimate shall, as soon as may be practicable after the expiry of two years from the date of the imposition of the levy, be revised in the manner provided in sub-sections (1) and (2) for the preparation, publication, and acceptance of an estimate.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Fixing value of increased outturn</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">9. The Government shall, by notification, fix annually or for such period not exceeding five years as may be specified in the notification the price or prices on the basis of which the value of the average increase in the outturn, as estimated under section 8 from land of any class in a notified area is to be calculated.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Maximum limit and incidence of improvement levy</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">10.(1) Notwithstanding anything contained in any other Act the improvement levy shall be imposed in respect of agricultural lands within a notified area at such rate or rates as the Government may, by notification, from time to time declare, and different rates may be so declared for classes of land of different descriptions or having different advantages:</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Provided that any rate so fixed shall not exceed one half of the estimated net increase, resulting from the improvement work, in the profit or one half of the net value of the estimated increase in outturn.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Such improvement levy shall be payable by the occupiers of such lands within the notified area.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Explanation.-In this sub-section the expression "estimated increase in outturn" means the average increase in the outturn of agricultural produce as estimated under section 8.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The rate or rates of the improvement levy shall be fixed under sub-section (1) for one year or for such period not exceeding five years as may be specified in the notification issued under that sub-section.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) For the purposes of sub-section (1) the net increase in the profits and the net value of the estimated increase in outturn shall be estimated, in accordance with rules made under this Act on the price or prices fixed under section 9.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(4) The Government may, by rules made under this Act, declare what persons or classes of persons shall be deemed, for the purposes of sub-section (1), to be occupiers of land but no person shall, by such rules, be declared to be an occupier of land unless, otherwise than as a hired labourer, he cultivates such land or (if it is not cultivated) unless he is in direct possession of such land.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(5) Notwithstanding anything contained in sub-section (4), where a person under the system generally knows as "adhi", "barga" or "bhag", cultivates the land of another person on condition of delivering a share of the produce to that person or receiving a share thereof from him, the person whose land is cultivated and the person who cultivates it shall each be deemed, for the purposes of sub-section (1), to be an occupier of such land, and each shall be liable to pay a prescribed proportion of the improvement levy imposed in respect of such land, and any contract to the contrary shall, to that extent, be void.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Additional improvement levy in certain cases</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">11. (1) Notwithstanding anything contained in section 10, if in any notified area, any unculturable waste, swamp, or sand has, as a result of an improvement work, become culturable land, and such land is thereafter settled with any tenant, the person who settles the land shall be liable to pay, in one sum, an improvement levy of such amount as may be fixed by the Collector, in accordance with rules made under this Act, after considering any objection that may be made in the prescribed manner by such person.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The amount fixed under sub-section (1) shall not exceed one -half of the difference between-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) the amount which the Collector estimates to be the usual salami for a like area of land, in the vicinity, similar in its description and its advantages to the land as it is at the time of the settlement, and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) the amount which the Collector estimates to have been the usual salami before the commencement of the improvement work, for a like area of land, in the vicinity, similar in its description and its advantages to the land as it was at that time.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Such levy shall be additional to the levy payable under section 10 by the occupier of the land.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Amount of improvement levy after realisation of capital cost and other charges</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">12. When in respect of any improvement work-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) the capital cost of such work, including the cost of any extensions, improvement or modifications of the work.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) the interest charges on such capital cost.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c) any working loss in any year or years, and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d) the interest on such loss,</p><p style="text-align: justify;">as determined by the Government, have been recovered in full out of the proceeds of the improvement levy, by such annual allocations as may be prescribed, the amount of the improvement levy to be realised for each year in respect of such work shall thereafter be reduced to such a sum as the 10[ Parliament] may, by a resolution, recommend.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Explanation.-The term "working loss" means the sum by which the proceeds of the improvement levy in any year or years fall short of the amount necessary to meet-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(i) the annual allocations for such year or years in respect of the charges specified in clauses (a) and (b), and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(ii) the cost, as determined by the Government, of maintenance and supervision of the improvement work, and of collection of the improvement levy, during such year or years.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Preparation and publication of statements of imposition of improvement levy</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">13. The Collector shall, from time to time, prepare and publish in the prescribed form and manner for a notified area or any part thereof a statement showing-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(i) the name of every person who is liable to pay the improvement levy in respect of any land in such area or part, and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(ii) the amount of improvement levy to be paid by each such person, annually or otherwise, in respect of such land.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Notice of demand</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">14. The Collector shall serve a notice of demand in the prescribed form and manner and containing the prescribed particulars, on every person whose name appears in a statement published under section 13 requiring him to pay the levy by such date or dates as may be specified in the notice.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Republication of statements and revised notice of demand</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">15.(1) After forty days from the date of publication of a statement under section 13, the Collector shall, in accordance with rules made under this Act, republish the statement with such modifications as he may have made as a result of representations by persons whose names were included therein, and, subject to any decisions, by an appellate or revisional authority, all entries in the statement as thus republished shall be presumed to be correct in every particular for the purposes of this Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) If the Collector makes any modification referred to in sub-section (1) in the statement he shall serve on the person concerned a revised notice of demand in the prescribed form and manner and containing the prescribed particulars.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Supplementary statements</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">16.(1) The Collector may from time to time, add to or alter in the prescribed manner any statement republished under sub-section (1) of section 15. In such case, the Collector shall publish in the prescribed form and manner a supplementary statement showing any addition or alteration so made, and the provisions of this Act shall apply to such supplementary statement as if it were a statement published under section 13.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) Where any addition to or alteration in a statement is required as a result of a decision of an appellate or revisional authority, the Collector shall add to or alter the statement accordingly, and it shall not be necessary to publish any supplementary statement in respect thereof under sub-section (1).</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Appeals in regard to improvement levy</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">17.(1) Any person may appeal within thirty days from the date of service of the notice under section 14 or of a revised notice, if any, under sub-section (2) of section 15 or from the date of republication of a statement under sub-section (1) of section 15, whichever is later, to the Commissioner of the Division, on the ground that he has been wrongly shown in the statement as liable to pay the improvement levy or that the amount shown in such statement as payable by him is incorrect, and the decision of the Commissioner of the Division on such appeal shall, subject to the provision of sub-section (2), be final.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The 11[ Government] may, on application made within thirty days from the date of the order of the Commissioner of the Division, revise such order.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Bar to objections to improvement levy, except as provided in this Act</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">18. No objection shall be taken to the imposition of an improvement levy, nor shall the liability of any person to pay the same be questioned, in any other manner than that provided in this Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Copies of entries in statement</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">19. Copies of entries in a statement published under section 13 or republished under sub-section (1) of section 15 shall be made available in the prescribed manner on payment of the prescribed fee.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Power of Collector to grant abatement or remission of improvement levy</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">20. Notwithstanding anything contained in this Act, the Collector may, subject to rules made by the Government at any time grant abatement or remission of the improvement levy payable under this Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Collection of improvement levy</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">21.(1) Subject to the provision of section 20, the Collector shall, in the prescribed manner, collect from any person whose name appears in a statement republished under sub-section (1) of section 15 the amount shown therein as due from him together with any interest payable under sub-section (2).</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) If any amount of improvement levy due from any person is not paid on or before the prescribed date, interest at such rate, not exceeding six and a quarter percent, per annum, as the Government may fix from time to time shall be payable thereon from the date of the default.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Refunds</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">22. If any person has paid any amount as improvement levy which, in accordance with the decision of the appellate or revisional authority, or in the opinion of the Collector, was not payable by such person, the Collector shall, in the prescribed manner, refund the amount to such person.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Recovery of arrears and other dues</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">23. All arrears of improvement levy, together with interest due thereon, and other dues payable to the Government under this Act shall be recoverable as public demands.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Power to enter on land and to cut and remove crops</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">24.(1) If, in the opinion of the Government it is desirable for the purpose of collecting information regarding the outturn of produce from any agricultural land, the Government may, by general or special order, authorize any officer and his servants and workmen, subject to rules made under this Act, to enter upon any land and to do any acts necessary for the purpose of obtaining such information:</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Provided that no person shall enter into any building or upon any enclosed courtyard or garden attached to a dwelling house (except with the consent of the occupier thereof) without previously giving such occupier at least seven days' notice in writing of his intention to do so.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) If, in the opinion of any officer authorized under sub-section (1), it is necessary to remove any crop for the purpose of ascertaining, by weighment or otherwise, the amount of the produce derived from any land, he may, subject to rules made under this Act, and after giving notice in writing, forthwith take possession of any standing crop on such land or part thereof, and may cause such crop to be cut and to be removed within such reasonable period a he may consider necessary.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) In every case under sub-section (2), such officer shall offer to the persons interested compensation for the standing crop cut and, subject to rules made under this Act, for any other damage caused during the process of cutting and removal; and, if such offer is not accepted the value of the crop cut and the amount of the damage so caused shall be assessed by the Collector in the prescribed manner.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Power to compel production of statements and documents</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">25.(1) Subject to rules made under this Act, any officer authorized under sub-section (1) of section 24 may, by notice, require any person to make and deliver to him a statement or to produce records or documents in his possession or control relating to any land mentioned in that sub-section, at a time and place specified in the notice.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) Every person required to make or deliver a statement</p><p style="text-align: justify;">or to produce any record or document under this section shall be</p><p style="text-align: justify;">deemed legally bound to do so within the meaning of sections 175 and 176 of the 12[ Penal Code].</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Power of Collector to enforce attendance of witnesses and production of documents</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">26. For the purposes of any inquiry under this Act the Collector shall have power to summon and enforce the attendance of witnesses, including the persons interested or any of them, and to compel the production of documents by the same means and, so far as may be, in the same manner as is provided in the case of a Civil Court under the Code of Civil Procedure, 1908.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Dues payable under other Acts in respect of improvement work</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">27. (1) Notwithstanding anything contained in any other Act, no person who has been declared liable to pay an improvement levy in respect of any land benefited by an improvement work shall be liable to pay any rates, dues or charges to the Government under any of the Acts mentioned in the schedule in return for any benefit derived by such land from the improvement work.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) When an improvement levy is imposed under this Act in any area in respect of an irrigation work and an agreement exists for the supply of water under the Irrigation Act, 1876, to any land in that area, the improvement levy shall not be payable in respect of such land until the expiry of the agreement.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Supply of water and application of rules under the Irrigation Act, 1876</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">28. (1) Within a notified area water may be supplied from a canal to any land not withstanding the fact that no application has been made under section 74 of the Irrigation Act, 1876.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) In any notified area specified by the Government, by notification, in this behalf any person by whom an improvement levy is payable under section 10 shall, subject to the provisions of sub-section (1) of section 27, be bound by any rules made under the Irrigation Act, 1876, for the time being in force, as if he had presented an application under section 74 of the said Act and such application had been granted.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Right to supply of water</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">29. Notwithstanding anything contained in the Irrigation Act, 1876, no person shall have a right to a supply of water</p><p style="text-align: justify;">under that Act in a notified area within any period prescribed in this behalf.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Power to carry out drainage work</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">30. Whenever it appears expedient to carry out any scheme of drainage for the betterment of public health or for the improvement of any land or in connection with irrigation works, the Government may, after issuing a notification and, in the prescribed manner, calling for and considering objections, if any, cause such a scheme to be drawn up and carried into execution, and any officer authorised in this behalf by the Government may exercise in connection with such scheme all or any of the powers conferred on Canal Officers by sections 33, 34 and 35 of the Irrigation Act, 1876, and thereupon the provisions of sections 36, 37 and 38 of that Act shall be applicable as if such officer were a Canal Officer.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Power to prohibit, remove or modify obstructions to the passage of water in channels</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">31. The Government may, if it is of opinion that in any area to be specified in a notification the hole or part of any river, stream, natural water-channel or natural drainage-course should be open to the unrestricted passage of water, exercise such powers as may be exercised under the Irrigation Act, 1876, with regard to the prohibition, removal or modification of obstructions in any river, stream, natural water channel or natural drainage-course, and the provisions contained in the Act with regard to and, subject to the provisions of section 35, incidental to exercise of such powers shall be applicable mutatis mutandis so far as they may reasonably be applied.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Power to modify obstructions to the passage of water through or over land</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">32.(1) The Government may, by notification, declare that in any area specified in the notification every person shall be bound, for irrigation purpose or for the drainage of land which has been irrigated, to afford a free passage to water through or over any land in his possession or under his control.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) After the issue of a notification under sub-section (1) the Collector, if in his opinion the free passage of water through or over any land in such area is necessary for irrigation purposes or for the drainage of land which has been irrigated, may, subject to rules made under this Act, from time to time, issue a general or special order upon persons who have such land in their possession or under their control to modify, in such manner and within such period as may be specified in the order, any artificial obstruction that exists on such land to such free passage, or to show cause against such order.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) If the Collector is not satisfied with any cause that may have been shown, he shall fix a further period within which the obstruction shall be modified.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(4) If any person fails to comply with an order under sub-section (2) or sub-section (3), or under section 37, in respect of such modification, he shall be liable on conviction by a magistrate to a fine not exceeding fifty 13[ Taka] for each such offence, and to a further fine not exceeding five 14[ Taka] for each day after conviction during which the obstruction remains unmodified, and the Collector may cause the obstruction to be modified and may recover the cost of modification from such person.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Notification of dead or decayed rivers</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">33.(1) The Government may, from time to time, publish by notification a list of rivers or depression which it intends to declare to be dead or decayed rivers.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) In any list published under sub-section (1) any river or depression may be described either by name or by reference to its geographical situation.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) After the expiry of a period for objection to be mentioned in a notification under sub-section (1), the Government shall consider the objections and suggestions, if any, received by it and thereafter may, by notification, declare any river or depression notified under that sub-section to be a dead or decayed river, and such declaration shall be final and shall not be questioned in any Court or in any other manner whatsoever.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Limitation of claims for compensation</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">34. No person shall be entitled to claim any compensation under this or any other Act for any injury, damage or less caused by a damage or decayed river which has been revived as a result of an improvement work, or by any other rivers into which it flows or spills, unless the injury, damage or loss is such as would have rendered the Government liable to pay compensation had the river not been revived.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Explanation.-A dead or decayed river is said to be revived when an increased volume of water is, by any means whatsoever, caused to flow freely into or along any part of such dead or decayed river.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Claims for compensation</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">35. Subject to the provisions of section 34, whenever-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) any damage is caused as a result of the prohibition, removal or modification of an obstruction under section 31 or section 32, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) any land or right of property is injuriously affected by any improvement work in respect of which an improvement levy is imposed under this Act,</p><p style="text-align: justify;">the person by whom any damage or loss is sustained shall not be entitled to claim any compensation for such damage or loss under any other Act, but such person may, not later than six months after the first occurrence of the injury in respect of which the claim is preferred, prefer to the Collector a claim for compensation.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Determination of amount of compensation</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">36.(1) When a claim is preferred under section 35, the Collector shall, in the prescribed manner, after such inquiry as he deems proper and after considering any representations which may be made to him determine the amount of compensation, if any, which shall be granted.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) In determining whether any and, if so, what amount of compensation shall be granted, the Collector shall be bound by the provisions of any rules made by the Government under this Act regulating the grant of compensation under this section.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) When the amount of compensation has been determined under sub-section (1), if any dispute arises as to the apportionment of the same or any part thereof, the Collector shall, in the prescribed manner, refer such dispute to the Court, and such Court or any other Court mentioned in sub-section (5) to which the dispute may, subject to rules made under this Act, be transferred for decision, shall decide the same.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(4) In every reference under sub-section (3) the costs shall be at the discretion of the Court.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(5) In this section "Court" means a principal Civil Court of original jurisdiction and includes the Court of any Additional Judge, Subordinate Judge or 15[ Assistant Judge] whom the</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Government may appoint, by name or by virtue of his office, to perform concurrently with any such principal Civil Court the functions of the Court under this section within any specified local limits and, in the case of a 16[ Assistant Judge] up to the limits of the pecuniary jurisdiction with which he is vested under section 19 of the 17[ Civil Courts Act, 1887].</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Appeals for certain decisions and orders of Collector</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">37.(1) Any person aggrieved by decision or order of the Collector under section 20, sub-section (3) of section 24, section 32 or sub-section (1) of section 36 may appeal, within thirty days from the date of such decision or order, to the Commissioner of the Division, whose decision on such appeal shall, subject to the provisions of sub-section (2), be final.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The 18[ Government] may, on application made within thirty days from the date of the order of the Commissioner of the Division, revise such order.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Costs</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">38. In every appeal under sub-section (1) of section 17, or under sub-section (1) of section 37, and in every revision under sub-section (2) of section 17 or under sub-section (2) of section 37, the costs shall be at the discretion of the appellate or revisional authority, and such costs shall be recoverable as a public demand.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Restrictions on enhancement of rent of agricultural lands in notified area</p><p style="text-align: justify;">39. 19[ * * *] when an improvement levy has been imposed in respect of any agricultural land-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) the rent payable for such land at the time of the imposition of the levy or fixed thereafter in accordance with the provisions of clause (b) shall not be enhanced on account of-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(i) benefits derived from the construction of any improvement work, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(ii) an increase in the productive powers of the land due to fluvial action;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) if a settlement is made of such land with a tenant thereafter, the rate of rent at which such land is settled shall not exceed the average rate of money rent payable, at the time of such settlement, by tenants of a similar class for land of a similar description and with similar advantages in the vicinity, and any rent in excess of such rate shall not be recoverable:</p><p style="text-align: justify;">20[ * * *]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">A stipulation in any contract by which a tenant taking settlement of such land agrees to pay any amount in excess of such rent, otherwise than as salami, shall not be binding on such tenant to the extent of such excess.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Publication of notifications</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">40. The Government shall cause every notification under this Act to be published in such manner and as such places as it thinks fit.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Proceedings not to be invalidated by irregularities</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">41. No proceedings under this Act shall be defeated or invalidated by reason of any defect or omission in the publication or service of any notification, statement, notice or order, unless material injury is done to any person by such defect or omission.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Bar to suits for compensation</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">42. No suit shall lie in any Civil Court for compensation in respect of any injury, damage or loss resulting from an improvement work or from anything done under this Act,</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Indemnity</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">43. No suit or other legal proceeding shall lie against any person for anything which is in good faith done or intended to be done under this Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Rules</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">44. (1) The Government may, subject to the condition of previous publication, make rules for carrying out the purposes of this Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) In particular and without prejudice to the generality</p><p style="text-align: justify;">of the foregoing power, the Government may make rules to</p><p style="text-align: justify;">provide for all or any of the following matters, namely:-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) the manner in which the average increase in the outturn of agricultural produce shall be estimated under section 8 and the manner of hearing objections under sub-section (1) of that section;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) the persons or classes of persons who shall, for the purposes of sub-section(1) of section 10, be deemed to be occupiers of land;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c) the manner in which the net increase in the profits and the net value of the estimated increase in outturn shall be estimated under sub-section (3) of section 10;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d) the proportion of improvement levy payable under sub-section (5) of section 10 by different classes of "adhiars", "bargadars", or 'bhagdars" and by the persons whose land is cultivated by such "adhiars", "bargadars", or 'bhagdars";</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(e) the determination of the amount of improvement levy payable under section 11 and the manner in which objections under sub-section (1) of that section shall be made;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(f) the annual allocations to be made under section 12 in respect of each improvement work;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(g) the form and manner of preparation and publication of a statement under section 13 and its republication under sub-section (1) of section 15;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(h) the form and contents of the notice of demand under section 14 and of a revised notice of demand under sub-section (2) of section 15 and the manner of service of such notice;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(i) the manner in which a statement republished under sub-section (1) of section 15 may be added to or altered, and the form and manner of publication of a supplementary statement under section 16.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(j) the procedure to be followed by the appellate and revisional authorities mentioned in sections 17 and 37;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(k) the manner of, and the amount of fees payable for, supplying copies under section 19;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(l) the grant of abatement or remission of the improvement levy under section 20;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(m) the manner of collection of the improvement levy and interest under sub-section (1) of section 21;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(n) the date of payment of improvement levy under sub-section (2) of section 21;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(o) the manner of refund of improvement levy under section 22;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(p) the procedure and conduct of officers and persons authorised under sub-sections (1) and (2) of Section 24;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(q) the offer of compensation, and the manner of assessment by the Collector of damage, under sub-section (3) of section 24.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(r) the exercise of powers under sub-section (1) of section 25 to enforce the making and delivery of statements and production of documents;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(s) the period within which persons shall not have any right to a supply of water under section 29.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(t) the manner in which objections shall be called for and dealt with under section 30;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(u) the issue of order under sub-section (2) of section 32 for the modification of obstructions to the free passage of water through or over land;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(v) the procedure to be followed by the Collector under sub-section (1) and sub-section (3) of section 36;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(w) the transfer of disputes for decision under sub-section (3) of section 36; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(x) the grant of compensation under section 36.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">____________________________________________________</p><p
