(1) Subject to the provisions of section 22, the act of a partner which is done to carry on, in the usual way, business of the kind carried by the firm, binds the firm.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">The authority of a partner to bind the firm conferred by this section is called his "implied authority".</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) In the absence of any usage or custom of trade to the contrary, the implied authority of a partner does not empower him to-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) submit a dispute relating to the business of the firm to arbitration,</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) open a banking account on behalf of the firm in his own name,</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c) compromise or relinquish any claim or portion of a claim by the firm,</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d) withdraw a suit or proceeding filed on behalf of the firm,</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(e) admit any liability in a suit or proceeding against the firm,</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(f) acquire immovable property on behalf of the firm,</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(g) transfer immovable property belonging to the firm, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(h) enter into partnership on behalf of the firm.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Extension and restriction of partner's implied authority</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">20. The partners in a firm may, by contract between the partners, extend or restrict the implied authority of any partner.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Notwithstanding any such restriction, any act done by a partner on behalf of the firm which falls within his implied authority binds the firm, unless the person with whom he is dealing knows of the restriction or does not know or believe that partner to be a partner.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Partner's authority in an emergency</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">21. A partner has authority, in an emergency, to do all such acts for the purpose of protecting the firm from loss as would be done by a person of ordinary prudence, in his own case, acting under similar circumstances, and such acts bind the firm.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Mode of doing act to bind firm</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">22. In order to bind a firm, an act or instrument done or executed by a partner or other person on behalf of the firm shall be done or executed in the firm name, or in any other manner expressing or implying an intention to bind the firm.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Effect of admissions by a partner</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">23. An admission or representation made by a partner concerning the affairs of the firm is evidence against the firm, if it is made in the ordinary course of business.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Effect of notice to acting partner</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">24. Notice to a partner who habitually acts in the business of the firm of any matter relating to the affairs of the firm operates as notice to the firm, except in the case of a fraud on the firm committed by or with the consent of that partner.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Liability of a partner for acts of the firm</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">25. Every partner is liable, jointly with all the other partners and also severally, for all acts of the firm done while he is a partner.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Liability of the firm for wrongful acts of a partner</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">26. Where, by the wrongful act or omission of a partner acting in the ordinary course of the business of a firm, or with the authority of his partners, loss or injury is caused to any third party, or any penalty is incurred, the firm is liable therefor to the same extent as the partner.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Liability of firm for misapplication by partners</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">27. Where-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) a partner acting within his apparent authority receives money or property from a third party and misapplies it, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) a firm in the course of its business receives money or property from a third party, and the money or property is misapplied by any of the partners while it is in the custody of the firm,</p><p style="text-align: justify;">the firm is liable to make good the loss.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Holding out</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">28.(1) Anyone who by words spoken or written or by conduct represents himself, or knowingly permits himself to be represented, to be a partner in a firm, is liable as a partner in that firm to anyone who has on the faith of any such representation given credit to the firm, whether the person representing himself or represented to be a partner does or does not know that the representation has reached the person so giving credit.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) Where after a partner's death the business is continued in the old firm name, the continued use of that name or of the deceased partner's name as a part thereof shall not of itself make his legal representative or his estate liable for any act of the firm done after his death.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Rights of transferee of a partner's interest</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">29. (1) A transfer by a partner of his interest in the firm either absolute or by mortgage, or by the creation by him of a charge on such interest, does not entitle the transferee, during the continuance of the firm, to interfere in the conduct of the business, or to require accounts, or to inspect the books of the firm, but entitles the transferee only to receive the share of profits of the transferring partner, and the transferee shall accept the account of profits agreed to by the partners.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) If the firm is dissolved or if the transferring partner ceases to be a partner, the transferee is entitled as against the remaining partners to receive the share of the assets of the firm to which the transferring partner is entitled, and, for the purpose of ascertaining that share, to an account as from the date of the dissolution.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Minors admitted to the benefits of partnership</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">30. (1) A person who is a minor according to the law to which he is subject may not be a partner in a firm, but, with the consent of all the partners for the time being, he may be admitted to the benefits of partnership.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) Such minor has a right to such share of the property and of the profits of the firm as may be agreed upon, and he may have access to and inspect and copy any of the accounts of the firm.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) Such minor's share is liable for the acts of the firm, but the minor is not personally liable for any such act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(4) Such minor may not sue the partners for an account or payment of his share of the property or profits of the firm, save when severing his connection with the firm, and in such case the amount of his share shall be determined by a valuation made as far as possible in accordance with the rules contained in section 48:</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Provided that all the partners acting together or any partners entitled to dissolve the firm upon notice to other partners may elect in such suit to dissolve the firm, and thereupon the Court shall proceed with the suit as one for dissolution and for settling accounts between the partners, and the amount of the share of the minor shall be determined along with the shares of the partners.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(5) At any time within six months of his attaining majority, or of his obtaining knowledge that he had been admitted to the benefits of partnership, whichever date is later, such person may give public notice that he has elected to become or that he has elected not to become a partner in the firm, and such notice shall determine his position as regards the firm:</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Provided that, if he fails to give such notice, he shall become a partner in the firm on the expiry of the said six months.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(6) Where any person has been admitted as a minor to the benefits of partnership in a firm, the burden of proving the fact that such person had no knowledge of such admission until a particular date after the expiry of six months of his attaining majority shall lie on the persons asserting that fact.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(7) Where such person becomes a partner,-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) his rights and liabilities as a minor continue up to the date on which he becomes a partner, but he also becomes personally liable to third parties for all acts of the firm done since he was admitted to the benefits of partnership, and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) his share in the property and profits of the firm shall be the share to which he was entitled as a minor.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(8) Where such person elects not to become a partner,-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) his rights and liabilities shall continue to be those of a minor under this section up to the date on which he gives public notice,</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) his share shall not be liable for any acts of the firm done after the date of the notice, and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c) he shall be entitled to sue the partners for his share of the property and profits in accordance with sub-section (4).</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(9) Nothing in sub-sections (7) and (8) shall affect the provisions of section 28.</p><p align="center">CHAPTER V</p><p align="center">INCOMING AND OUTGOING PARTNERS</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Introduction of a partner</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">31. (1) Subject to contract between the partners and to the provisions of section 30, no person shall be introduced as a partner into a firm without the consent of all the existing partners.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) Subject to the provisions of section 30, a person who is introduced as a partner into a firm does not thereby become liable for any act of the firm done before he become a partner.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Retirement of a partner</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">32. (1) A partner may retire-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) with the consent of all the other partners,</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) in accordance with an express agreement by the partners, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c) where the partnership is at will, by giving notice in writing to all the other partners of his intention to retire.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) A retiring partner may de discharged from any liability to any third party for acts of the firm done before his retirement by an agreement made by him with such third party and the partners of the reconstituted firm, and such agreement may be implied by a course of dealing between such third party and the reconstituted firm after he had knowledge of the retirement.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) Notwithstanding the retirement of a partner from a firm, he and the partners continue to be liable as partners to third parties for any act done by any of them which would have been an act of the firm if done before the retirement, until public notice is given of the retirement:</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Provided that a retired partner is not liable to any third party who deals with the firm without knowing that he was a partner.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(4) Notice under sub-section (3) may be given by the retired partner or by any partner of the reconstituted firm.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Expulsion of a partner</p><p style="text-align: justify;">33. (1) A partner may not be expelled from a firm by any majority of the partners, save in the exercise in good faith of powers conferred by contract between the partners.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The provisions of sub-sections (2), (3) and (4) of section 32 shall apply to an expelled as if he were retired partner.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Insolvency of a partner</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">34.(1) Where a partner in a firm is adjudicated an insolvent he ceases to be a partner on the date on which the order of adjudication is made, whether or not the firm is thereby dissolved.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) Where under a contract between the partners the firm is not dissolved by the adjudication of a partner as an insolvent, the estate of a partner so adjudicated is not liable for any act of the firm and the firm is not liable for any act of the insolvent, done after the date on which the order of adjudication is made.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Liability of estate of deceased partner</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">35. Where under a contract between the partners the firm is not dissolved by the death of a partner, the estate of a deceased partner is not liable for any act of the firm done after his death.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Rights of outgoing partner to carry on competing business</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">36.(1) An outgoing partner may carry on a business competing with that of the firm and he may advertise such business, but, subject to contract to the contrary, he may not-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        use the firm name,</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        represent himself as carrying on the business of the firm, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c)        solicit the custom of persons who were dealing with the firm before he ceased to be a partner.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Agreements in restraint of trade</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) A partner may make an agreement with his partners that on ceasing to be a partner he will not carry on any business similar to that of the firm within a specified period or within specified local limits; and, notwithstanding anything contained in section 27 of the Contract Act, 1872, such agreement shall be valid if the restrictions imposed are reasonable.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Right of outgoing partner in certain cases to share subsequent profits</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">37. Where any member of a firm has died or otherwise ceased to be a partner, and the surviving or continuing partners carry on the business of the firm with the property of the firm without any final settlement of accounts as between them and the outgoing partner or his estate, then, in the absence of a contract to the contrary, the outgoing partner or his estate is entitled at the option of himself or his representatives to such share of the profits made since he ceased to be a partner as may be attributable to the use of his share of the property of the firm or to interest at the rate of six per cent. per annum on the amount of his share in the property of the firm:</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Provided that where by contract between the partners an option is given to surviving or continuing partners to purchase the interest of a deceased or outgoing partner, and that option is duly exercised, the estate of the deceased partner or the outgoing partner or his estate as the case may be, is not entitled to any further or other share of profits; but if any partner assuming to act in exercise of the option does not in all material respects comply with the terms thereof, he is liable to account under the foregoing provisions of this section.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Revocation of continuing guarantee by change in firm</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">38. A continuing guarantee given to a firm, or to a third party in respect of the transactions of a firm, is, in the absence of agreement to the contrary, revoked as to future transactions from the date of any change in the constitution of the firm.</p><p align="center">CHAPTER VI</p><p align="center">DISSOLUTION OF A FIRM</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Dissolution of a firm</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">39. The dissolution of partnership between all the partners of a firm is called the "dissolution of the firm".</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Dissolution by agreement</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">40. A firm may be dissolved with the consent of all the partners or in accordance with a contract between the partners</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Compulsory dissolution</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">41. A firm is dissolved-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        by the adjudication of all the partners or of all the partners but one as insolvent, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        by the happening of any event which makes it unlawful for the business of the firm to be carried on or for the partners to carry it on in partnership:</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Provided that, where more than one separate adventure or undertaking is carried on by the firm, the illegality of one or more shall not of itself cause the dissolution of the firm in respect of its lawful adventures and undertakings.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Dissolution on the happening of certain contingencies</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">42. Subject to contract between the partners a firm is dissolved-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        if constituted for a fixed term, by the expiry of that term;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        if constituted to carry out one or more adventures or undertakings, by the completion thereof;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c)        by the death of a partner; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d)        by the adjudication of a partner as an insolvent.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Dissolution by notice of partnership at will</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">43.(1) Where the partnership is at will, the firm may be dissolved by any partner giving notice in writing to all the other partners of his intention to dissolve the firm.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The firm is dissolved as from the date mentioned in the notice as the date of dissolution or, if no date is so mentioned, as from the date of the communication of the notice.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Dissolution by the Court</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">44. At the suit of a partner, the Court may dissolve a firm on any of the following grounds, namely:-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) that a partner has become of unsound mind, in which case the suit may be brought as well by the next friend of the partner who has become of unsound mind as by any other partner;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) that a partner, other than the partner suing, has become in any way permanently incapable of performing his duties as partner;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c) that a partner, other than the partner suing, is guilty of conduct which is likely to affect prejudicially the carrying on of the business, regard being had to the nature of the business;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d) that a partner, other than the partner suing, wilfully or persistently commits breach of agreements relating to the management of the affairs of the firm or the conduct of its business, or otherwise so conducts himself in matters relating to the business that it is not reasonably practicable for the other partners to carry on the business in partnership with him;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(e) that a partner, other than the partner suing, has in any way transferred the whole of his interest in the firm to a third party, or has allowed his share to be charged under the provisions of rule 49 of Order XXI of the First Schedule to the Code of Civil Procedure, 1908, or has allowed it to be sold in the recovery of arrears of land-revenue or of any dues recoverable as arrears of land-revenue due by the partner;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(f) that the business of the firm cannot be carried on save at a loss; or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(g) on any other ground which renders it just and equitable that the firm should be dissolved.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Liability for acts of partners done after dissolution</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">45.(1) Notwithstanding the dissolution of a firm, the partners continue to be liable as such to third parties for any act done by any of them which would have been an act of the firm if done before the dissolution, until public notice is given of the dissolution:</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Provided that the estate of a partner who dies, or who is adjudicated an insolvent, or of a partner who, not having been known to the person dealing with the firm to be a partner, retires from the firm, is not liable under this section for acts done after the date on which he ceases to be a partner.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) Notices under sub-section (1) may be given by any partner.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Right of partners to have business wound up after dissolution</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">46. On the dissolution of a firm every partner or his representative is entitled, as against all the other partners or their representatives, to have the property of the firm applied in payment of the debts and liabilities of the firm, and to have the surplus distributed among the partners or their representatives</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Continuing authority of partners for purposes of winding up</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">47. After the dissolution of a firm the authority of each partner to bind the firm, and the other mutual rights and obligations of the partners, continue notwithstanding the dissolution, so far as may be necessary to wind up the affairs of the firm and to complete transactions begun but unfinished at the time of the dissolution, but not otherwise:</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Provided that the firm is in no case bound by the acts of a partner who has been adjudicated insolvent; but this proviso does not affect the liability of any person who has after the adjudication represented himself or knowingly permitted himself to be represented as a partner of the insolvent.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Mode of settlement of accounts between partners</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">48. In settling the accounts of a firm after dissolution, the following rules shall, subject to agreement by the partners, be observed:-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) Losses, including deficiencies of capital, shall be paid first out of profits, next out of capital, and, lastly if necessary, by the partners individually in the proportions in which they were entitled to share profits,</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) The assets of the firm, including any sums contributed by the partners to make up deficiencies of capital, shall be applied in the following manner and order:?</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(i) in paying the debts of the firm to third parties;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(ii) in paying to each partner rateably what is due to him from the firm for advances as distinguished from capital;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(iii) in paying to each partner rateably what in due to him on account of capital; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(iv) the residue, if any, shall be divided among the partners in the proportions in which they were entitled to share profits.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Payment of firm debts and of separate debts</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">49. Where there are joint debts due from the firm, and also separate debts due from any partner, the property of the firm shall be applied in the first instance in payment of the debts of the firm, and, if there is any surplus, then the share of each partner shall be applied in payment of his separate debts or paid to him. The separate property of any partner shall be applied first in the payment of his separate debts, and the surplus (if any) in the payment of the debts of the firm.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Personal profits earned after dissolution</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">50. Subject to contract between the partners, the provisions of clause (a) of section 16 shall apply to transactions by any surviving partner or by the representatives of a deceased partner, undertaken after the firm is dissolved on account of the death of a partner and before its affairs have been completely wound up:</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Provided that where any partner or his representative has bought the goodwill of the firm, nothing in this section shall affect his right to use the firm name.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Return of premium on premature dissolution</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">51. Where a partner has plaid a premium on entering into partnership for a fixed term, and the firm is dissolved before the expiration of that term otherwise than by the death of a partner, he shall be entitled to repayment of the premium or of such part thereof as may be reasonable, regard being had to the terms upon which he became a partner and to the length of time during which he was a partner, unless-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) the dissolution is mainly due to his own misconduct, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) the dissolution is in pursuance of an agreement containing no provision for the return of the premium or any part of it.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Rights where partnership contract is rescinded for fraud or misrepresentation</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">52. Where a contract creating partnership is rescinded on the ground of the fraud or misrepresentation of any of the parties thereto, the party entitled to rescind is, without prejudice to any other right, entitled-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) to a lien on, or a right of retention of, the surplus or the assets of the firm remaining after the debts of the firm have been paid, for any sum paid by him for the purchase of a share in the firm and for any capital contributed by him;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        to rank as a creditor of the firm in respect of any payment made by him towards the debts of the firm; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c)        to be indemnified by the partner or partners guilty of the fraud or misrepresentation against all the debts of the firm.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Rights to restrain from use of firm name or firm property</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">53. After a firm is dissolved, every partner or his representative may, in the absence of a contract between the partners to the contrary, restrain any other partner or his representative from carrying on a similar business in the firm name or from using any of the property of the firm for his own benefit, until the affairs of the firm have been completely wound up:</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Provided that where any partner or his representative has bought the goodwill of the firm, nothing in this section shall affect his right to use the firm name.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Agreements in restraint of trade</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">54. Partners may, upon or in anticipation of the dissolution of the firm, make an agreement that some or all of them will not carry on a business similar to that of the firm within a specified period or within specified local limits; and notwithstanding anything contained in section 27 of the Contract Act, 1872, such agreement shall be valid if the restrictions imposed are reasonable.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Sale of goodwill after dissolution</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">55.(1) In settling the accounts of a firm after dissolution the goodwill shall, subject to contract between the partners be included in the assets, and it may be sold either separately or along with other property of the firm.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Rights of buyer and seller of goodwill</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) Where the goodwill of a firm is sold after dissolution, a partner may carry on a business competing with that of the buyer and he may advertise such business, but, subject to agreement between him and the buyer, he may not?</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        use the firm name,</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        represent himself as carrying on the business of the firm, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c)        solicit the custom of persons who were dealing with the firm before its dissolution.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Agreements in restraint of trade</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) Any partner may, upon the sale of the goodwill of a firm, make an agreement with the buyer that such partner will not carry on any business similar to that of the firm within a specified period or within specified local limits, and, notwithstanding anything contained in section 27 of the Contract Act, 1872, such agreement shall be valid if the restrictions imposed are reasonable.</p><p align="center">CHAPTER VII</p><p align="center">REGISTRATION OF FIRMS</p>[Omitted]<p style="text-align: justify;">56. [Omitted by section 3 and 2nd Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973).]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Appointment of Registrars</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">57. (1) The Government may appoint Registrars of Firms for the purposes of this Act, and may define the areas within which they shall exercise their powers and perform their duties.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) Every Registrar shall be deemed to be a public servant within the meaning of section 21 of the 2[ Penal Code].</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Application for registration</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">58.(1) The registration of a firm may be effected at any time by sending by post or delivering to the Registrar of the area in which any place of business of the firm is situated or proposed to be situated, a statement in the prescribed form and accompanied by the prescribed fee, stating-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) the firm name,</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) the place or principal place of business of the firm,</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c) the names of any other places where the firm carries on business,</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d) the date when each partner joined the firm,</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(e) the names in full and permanent addresses of the partners, and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(f) the duration of the firm.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">The statement shall be signed by all the partners, or by their agents specially authorized in this behalf.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) Each person signing the statement shall also verify it in the manner prescribed.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">3[ 4[ (3) A firm name shall not contain any of the following words, namely:?</p><p style="text-align: justify;">State or words expressing or implying the sanction, approval or patronage of the Government or of the Bangabandhu, except when the Government signifies its consent to the use of such words as part of the firm name by order in writing.]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3A) A firm name shall not contain the name of the "United Nations" or its abbreviations through the use of its initial letters or of any subsidiary body set up by that body unless it has obtained the previous authorization of the Secretary-General of the United Nations in writing.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3B) A firm name shall not contain the name of the "World Health Organization" or its abbreviations through the use of its initial letters unless it has obtained the previous authorization of the Director-General in writing.]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Registration</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">59. When the Registrar is satisfied that the provisions of section 58 have been duly complied with, he shall record an entry of the statement in a register called the Register of Firms, and shall file the statement.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Recording or alterations in firm name and principal place of business</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">60.(1) When an alteration is made in the firm name or in the location of the principal place of business of a registered firm, a statement may be sent to the Registrar accompanied by the prescribed fee, specifying the alteration, and signed and verified in the manner required under section 58.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) When the Registrar is satisfied that the provisions of sub-section (1) have been duly complied with, he shall amend the entry relating to the firm in the Register of Firms in accordance with the statement, and shall file it along with the statement relating to the firm filed under section 59.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Noting of closing and opening of branches</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">61. When a registered firm discontinues business at any place or begins to carry on business at any place, such place not being its principal place of business, any partner or agent of the firm may send intimation thereof to the Registrar, who shall make a note of such intimation in the entry relating to the firm in the Register of Firms, and shall file the intimation along with the statement relating to the firm filed under section 59.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Noting of changes in names and addresses of partners</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">62. When any partner in a registered firm alters his name or permanent address, an intimation of the alteration may be sent by any partner or agent of the firm to the registrar, who shall deal with it in the manner provided in section 61.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Recording of changes in and dissolution of a firm</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">63.(1) When a change occurs in the constitution of a registered firm any incoming, continuing or outgoing partner, and when a registered firm is dissolved any person who was a partner immediately before the dissolution, or the agent of any such partner, or person specially authorized in this behalf, may give notice to the Registrar of such change or dissolution, specifying the date thereof; and the Registrar shall make a record of the notice in the entry relating to the firm in the Register of Firms, and shall file the notice along with the statement relating to the firm filed under section 59.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Recording of withdrawal of a minor</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) When a minor who has been admitted to the benefits of partnership in a firm attains majority and elects to become or not to become a partner, and the firm is then a registered firm, he, or his agent specially authorized in this behalf, may give notice to the Registrar that he has or has not become a partner, and the Registrar shall deal with the notice in the manner provided in sub-section (1).</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Rectification of mistakes</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">64.(1) The Registrar shall have power at all times to rectify any mistake in order to bring the entry in the Register of Firms relating to any firm into conformity with the documents relating to that firm filed under this Chapter.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) On application made by all the parties who have signed any document relating to a firm filed under this Chapter, the Registrar may rectify any mistake in such document or in the record or note thereof made in the Register of Firms.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Amendment of Register by order of Court</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">65. A court deciding any matter relating to a registered firm may direct that the Registrar shall make any amendment in the entry in the Register of Firms relating to such firm which is consequential upon its decision; and the Registrar shall amend the entry accordingly.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Inspection of Register and filed documents</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">66.(1) The Register of Firms shall be open to inspection by any person on payment of such fee as may be prescribed.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) All statements, notices and intimations filed under this Chapter shall be open to inspection, subject to such condition and on payment of such fee as may be prescribed.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Grant of copies</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">67. The Registrar shall on application furnish to any person, on payment of such fee as may be prescribed, a copy, certified under his hand, of any entry or portion thereof in the Register of Firms.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Rules of evidence</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">68.(1) Any statement, intimation or notice recorded or noted in the Register of Firms shall, as against any person by whom or on whose behalf such statement, intimation or notice was signed, be conclusive proof of any fact therein stated.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) A certified copy of an entry relating to a firm in the Register of Firms may be produced in proof of the fact of the registration of such firm, and of the contents of any statement, intimation or notice recorded or noted therein.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Effect of non-registration</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">69.(1) No suit to enforce a right arising from a contract or conferred by this Act shall be instituted in any Court by or on behalf of any person suing as a partner in a firm against the firm or any person alleged to be or to have been a partner in the firm unless the firm is registered and the person suing is or has been shown in the Register of Firms as a partner in the firm.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) No suit to enforce a right arising from a contract shall be instituted in any Court by or on behalf of a firm against any third party unless the firm is registered and the persons suing are or have been shown in the Register of Firms as partners in the firm.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) The provisions of sub-sections (1) and (2) shall apply also to a claim of set-off or other proceeding to enforce a right arising from a contract, but shall not effect-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        the enforcement of any right to sue for the dissolution</p><p style="text-align: justify;">of a firm or for accounts of a dissolved firm, or any right or power to realise the property of a dissolved firm, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        the powers of an official assignee, receiver or Court under the 5[ Insolvency (Dacca) Act, 1909, or the] Insolvency Act, 1920, to realise the property of an insolvent partner.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(4) This section shall not apply-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        to firms or to partners in firms which have no place of business in Bangladesh, or whose places of business in Bangladesh are situated in areas to which, by notification under section 56, this Chapter does not apply, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        to any suit or claim of set-off not exceeding one hundred Taka in value which, is not of a kind specified in the Second Schedule to the 6[ * * *] Small Cause Courts Act, 1887, or to any proceeding in execution or other proceeding incidental to or arising from any such suit or claim.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Penalty for furnishing false particulars</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">70. Any person who signs any statement, amending statement, notice or intimation under this Chapter containing any particular which he knows to be false or does not believe to be true, or containing particulars which he knows to be incomplete or does not believe to be complete, shall be punishable with imprisonment which may extend to three months, or with fine, or with both.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Power to make rules</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">71.(1) The Government may make rules prescribing the fees which shall accompany documents sent to the Register of Firms, or which shall be payable for the inspection of documents</p><p style="text-align: justify;">in the custody of the Register of Firms, or for copies from the Register of Firms:</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Provided that such fees shall not exceed the maximum fees specified in Schedule I.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The Government may also make rules-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) prescribing the form of statement submitted under section 58, and of the verification thereof;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) requiring statements, intimations and notices under sections 60, 61, 62 and 63 to be in prescribed form, and prescribing the form thereof;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c) prescribing the form of the Register of Firms, and the mode in which entries relating to firms are to be made therein, and the mode in which such entries are to be amended or notes made therein;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d) regulating the procedure of the Registrar when disputes arise;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(e) regulating the filing of documents received by the Registrar;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(f) prescribing conditions for the inspection of original documents;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(g) regulating the grant of copies;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(h) regulating the elimination of registers and documents;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(i) providing for the maintenance and form of an index to the Register of Firms; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(j) generally, to carry out the purposes of this Chapter.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) All rules made under this section shall be subject to the condition of previous publication.</p><p align="center" style="text-align: justify;">CHAPTER VIII</p><p align="center" style="text-align: justify;">SUPPLEMENTAL</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Mode of giving public notice</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">72. A public notice under this Act is given-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        where it relates to the retirement or expulsion of a partner from a registered firm, or to the dissolution of a registered firm, or to the election to become</p><p style="text-align: justify;">or not to become a partner in a registered firm by a person attaining majority who was admitted as a minor to the benefits of partnership, by notice to the Register of Firms under section 63, and by publication in the official Gazette and in at least one vernacular newspaper circulating in the district where the firm to which it relates has its place or principal place of business, and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        in any other case, by publication in the official Gazette and in at least one vernacular newspaper circulating in the district where the firm to which it relates has its place or principal place of business.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">[Repealed]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">73. [Repealed by section 2 and Schedule of the Repealing Act, 1938 (Act No. I of 1938).]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Savings</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">74. Nothing in this Act or any repeal effected thereby shall affect or be deemed to affect-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        any right, title, interest, obligation or liability already acquired, accrued or incurred before the commencement of this Act, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        any legal proceeding or remedy in respect of any such right, title, interest, obligation or liability or anything done or suffered before the commencement of this Act, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c)        anything done or suffered before the commencement of this Act, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d)        any enactment relating to partnership not expressly repealed by this Act, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(e)        any rule of insolvency relating to partnership, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(f)         any rule of law not inconsistent with this Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">______________________________________________</p><p style="text-align: justify;">1 Throughout this Act, except otherwise provided, the words `Bangladesh`, `Government` and `Taka` were substituted, for the words `Pakistan`, `Provincial Government` and `rupees` or `rupee` respectively by section 3 and 2nd Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973).</p><p style="text-align: justify;">2 The words `Penal Code` were substituted, for the words `Pakistan Penal Code` by section 3 and 2nd Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">3 Sub-sections (3), (3A) and (3B) were substituted for sub-section (3) by section 2 of the Partnership (Amendment) Act, 1949 (Act No. V of 1949).</p><p style="text-align: justify;">4 Sub-section (3) was substituted, for sub-section (3) by section 3 and 2nd Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973).</p><p style="text-align: justify;">5 The words, brackets, commas and figure `Insolvency (Dacca) Act, 1909, or the` were substituted, for the words, brackets and comma `Insolvency (Karachi Division and Dacca) Act, or the Provincial` by section 3 and 2nd Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973).</p><p style="text-align: justify;">6 The word `Provincial` was omitted by section 3 and 2nd Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973).</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Source : Ministry of Law, Justice and Parliamentary Affairs</p>                       </div></div>
179	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">THE PETROLEUM ACT, 1934 </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p align="center"> <strong>THE PETROLEUM ACT, 1934</strong></p><p align="center">(ACT NO. XXX OF 1934)</p><p align="right">[6th September, 1934]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">An Act to consolidate and amend the law relating to the import transport, storage, production, 2[ 3[ refining, blending or reclaiming by recycling], distribution and marketing] of petroleum and other inflammable substances.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">WHEREAS it is expedient to consolidate and amend the law relating to the import, transport, storage, production, 4[ 5[ refining, blending or reclaiming by recycling], distribution and marketing] of petroleum and other inflammable substances;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">It is hereby enacted as follows:-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Short title, extent and commencement </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1. (1) This Act may be called the Petroleum Act, 1934.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) It extends to the whole of Bangladesh.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) It shall come into force on such date as the Government may, by notification in the official Gazette, appoint.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Definitions </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">2. In this Act, unless there is anything repugnant in the subject or context,-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        "petroleum" means any liquid hydrocarbon or mixture</p><p style="text-align: justify;">of hydrocarbons, and any inflammable mixture (liquid, viscous or solid ) containing any liquid hydrocarbon;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">6[ (b)   "class I petroleum" means petroleum having its flashing-point below twenty-three degrees centi-grade;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(bb)      "class II petroleum" means petroleum having its flashing-point below sixty-one degrees but not below twenty-three degrees centigrade; ]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c)        "flashing-point" of any petroleum means the lowest temperature at which it yields a vapour which will give a momentary flash when ignited, determined in accordance with the provisions of Chapter II and the rules made thereunder;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d)        "to transport" means to move petroleum from one place to another within Bangladesh by land, sea or air 7[ ***];</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(e)        "to import" petroleum means to bring it into Bangladesh by land, sea or air 8[ * * *];</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(f)         "to store" petroleum means to keep it in any one place, but does not include any detention happening during the ordinary course of transport;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(g)        "motor conveyance" means any vehicle, vessel or aircraft for the conveyance of human beings, animals or goods, by land, water or air, in which petroleum is used to generate the motive power;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(h)        "prescribed" means prescribed by rules made under this Act 9[ ;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(i)         "oil marketing company" means a company, organisation or other person having right, under the</p><p style="text-align: justify;">authority of the Government or otherwise, of marketing petroleum in Bangladesh;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(j)         "agent", in relation to oil marketing company, means a person, including a firm and a company, appointed with approval of the Government by an oil marketing company to be its agent for dealing in 10[ class II] petroleum;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(k)        "dealer" means a person including a firm and a company, appointed with the approval of the Government by an oil marketing company to be a dealer for dealing in 11[ class I] petroleum; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(l)         "stockist" means a person, including a firm and a company, appointed with the approval of the Government by an oil marketing company to be a stockist for maintaining stock, and for distribution among the agents and dealers, of both 12[ class I and class II] petroleum.]</p><p align="center">CHAPTER I</p><p align="center">CONTROL OVER PETROLEUM</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Import, transport and storage of petroleum</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">3. (1) No one shall import, transport 13[ store or distribute] any petroleum save in accordance with the rules made under section 4.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) Save in accordance with the conditions of any licence for the purpose which he may be required to obtain by rules make</p><p style="text-align: justify;">under section 4, on one shall import any 14[ class I] petroleum, and no one shall transport 15[ , store or distribute] any petroleum.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Rules for the import, transport and storage of petroleum</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">4. The Government may make rules-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) prescribing places where petroleum may be imported and prohibiting its import elsewhere;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) regulating the import of petroleum;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c) prescribing the periods within which licences for the import of 16[ class I] petroleum shall be applied for, and providing for the disposal, by confiscation or otherwise, of any 17[ class I] petroleum in respect of which a licence has not been applied for within the prescribed period or has been refused and which has not been exported;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d) regulating the transport of petroleum;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(e) specifying the nature and condition of all receptacles and pipe-lines in which petroleum may be transported;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(f) regulating the places at which and prescribing the conditions subject to which petroleum may be stored;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(g) specifying the nature, situation and condition of all receptacles in which petroleum may be stored;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(h) prescribing the form and conditions of licences for the import of dangerous petroleum, and for the transport or storage of any petroleum, the manner in which applications for such licences shall be made, the authorities which may grant such licences and the fees which may be charged for such licences;    (i) determining in any class of cases whether a licence for the transport of petroleum shall be obtained by the consignor. consignee or carrier;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(j) providing for the granting of combined licences for the import, transport 18[ , storage and distribution] of petroleum, or for any two of such purposes;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(k) prescribing the proportion in which any specified poisonous substance may be added to petroleum, and prohibiting the import, transport or storage of petroleum in which the proportion of any specified poisonous substance exceeds the prescribed proportion; 19[ * * *]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">20[ (l) regulating the distribution of petroleum;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(m) prescribing the conditions for the appointment of, and the granting of the licences to, agents, dealers and stockist;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(n) prescribing the form and conditions of agreement between and agent, dealer or stockist and an oil marketing company;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(o) providing for cancellation or restoration of licences of an agent or a dealer and of agreement between an oil marketing company and an agent, dealer or stockist; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(p) generally, providing for any matter which in its opinion, in expedient for proper control over the import, transport, storage and distribution of petroleum.]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Production, refining and blending of petroleum</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">5. (1) No one shall produce, 21[ refine, blend or reclaim by recycling] petroleum save in accordance with the rules made under sub-section (2).</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The Government may make rules-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) prescribing the conditions subject to which petroleum may be produced, 22[ refined, blended or reclaimed by recycling] and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) regulating the removal of petroleum from places where it is produced 23[ refined, blended or reclaimed by recycling] and preventing the storage therein and removal therefrom, except as 24[ class I] petroleum of any petroleum which has not satisfied the prescribed tests.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Receptacles of class I petroleum to show a warning</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">6. All receptacles containing 25[ class I] petroleum shall have a stamped, embossed, painted or printed warning, either on the receptacles itself or, where that is impracticable, displayed near the receptacle, exhibiting in conspicuous characters the words "Petrol" or "Motor Spirit" or an equivalent warning of the 26[ class I] nature of the petroleum:</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Provided that this section shall not apply to-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) any securely stoppered glass, stoneware or metal receptacle of less than 27[ nine litres] capacity containing 28[ class I] petroleum which is not for sale, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) a tank incorporated in a motor conveyance, or attached to an internal combustion engine, and containing intended to be used to generate motive power for the motor conveyance or engine, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c) a pipe-line for the transport of petroleum, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d) any tank which is wholly underground,</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(e) any class of receptacles which the Government may, by notification in the official Gazette, exempt from the operation of this section.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>No licence needed for small stocks of class II petroleum not in bulk</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">7. Notwithstanding anything contained in this Chapter a person need not obtain a licence for the transport or storage of 29[ class II] petroleum if the total quantity in his possession at any one place does not exceed 30[ two thousand litres] and none of it is contained in a receptacles exceeding 31[ one thousand litres] in capacity.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>No licence needed for small quantities of class I petroleum</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">8. (1) Notwithstanding anything contained in this chapter, a person need not obtain a licence for the import, transport or storage of 32[ class I] petroleum not intended for sale if the total quantity in his possession does not exceed 33[ twenty-five litres].</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) 34[ Class I] petroleum possessed without a licence under this section shall be kept in securely stoppered receptacles of glass, stoneware or metal which shall not in the case of receptacles of glass or stoneware exceed 35[ one litre] in capacity or in the case of receptacles of metal 36[ twenty litres] in capacity.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Exemptions for motor conveyances and stationary engines</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">9. (1) The owner of a motor conveyance, who complies with requirements of the law for the time being in force relating to the registration and licencing of such conveyance and its driver or pilot and the owner of any stationary internal combustion engine, shall not be required to contain a licence-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) for the import, transport or storage of any petroleum contained in any fuel tank incorporated in the conveyance or attached to the internal combustion engine, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) for the transport or storage of 37[ class I] petroleum, not exceeding 38[ ninety litres] in quantity in addition to any quantity possessed under clause (a),</p><p style="text-align: justify;">provided the petroleum is intended to be used to generate motive power for the motor conveyance or engine:</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Provided further that the total quantity of 39[ class I] petroleum which may be stored without a licence under clause (b) shall not exceed 40[ ninety litres], notwithstanding that such owner may possess other motor conveyances or engines.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The 41[ class I] petroleum transported or stored without a licence under clause (b) of sub-section (1) shall be kept as provided in sub-section (2) of section 8, and, if it exceeds 42[ twenty-five litres] in quantity shall be stored in an isolated place which does not communicate with any room where any person resides or works or in any room where persons assemble.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>No licence needed by railway administration acting as carrier</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">10. Notwithstanding anything contained in this Chapter, 43[ the railway] administration, as defined in section 3 of the Railways Act, 1890, need not obtain any licence for the import or transport of any petroleum in its possession in its capacity as carrier.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Exemption</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">44[ 11. [Nothing in this Chapter shall apply to the storage transport and import of any petroleum which has its flashing point not below ninety-five degrees centigrade.]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>General power of exemption</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">12. The Government may, by notification in the official Gazette, exempt any petroleum specified in the notification from all or any of the provisions of this Chapter.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Inspection of places</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">13.(1) The Government may authorise any officer by name or by virtue of office to enter any place where petroleum is being imported, 45[ stored, distributed] produced, 46[ refined blended or reclaimed by recycling] or is under transport, and inspect all receptacles, plant and appliances used in connection with petroleum in order to ascertain if they are in accordance with the provisions of this Chapter and the rules made thereunder.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The Government may make rules regulating the procedure of officers authorised under this section.</p><p align="center">CHAPTER II</p><p align="center">THE TESTING OF PETROLEUM</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Inspection and sampling of petroleum</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">14.(1) The Government may, by notification in the official Gazette, authorize any officer by name or by virtue of office to enter any place where petroleum is being imported, transported, 47[ stored, distributed], produced, 48[ refined, blended or reclaimed by recycling] and to inspect and take samples for testing of any petroleum found therein.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The Government may make rules-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) regulating the taking of samples of petroleum for testing,</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) determining the cases in which payment shall be made for the value of samples taken, and the mode of payment, and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c) generally, regulating the procedure of officers exercising powers under this section.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Standard Test Apparatus</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">15. (1) A standard apparatus for determining the flashing point of petroleum shall be deposited with an officer to be appointed in this behalf by the Government, by notification the official Gazette.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) Such apparatus shall be engraved with the words "Standard Test Apparatus", and shall be verified and corrected form time to time and replaced when necessary, in accordance with rules made under section 21.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) The Standard Test Apparatus shall, on payment of the prescribed fee, be open to inspection at all reasonable times by any person wishing inspect to it.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Certification of other Test Apparatus</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">16.(1) The officer appointed under section 15 shall, on payment of the prescribed fee, if any, compare with the Standard Test Apparatus any apparatus for determining the flashing-point of petroleum which may be submitted to him for him for this purpose.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) If any apparatus is found by him to agree with the Standard Test Apparatus within prescribed limits, the officer shall engrave such apparatus with a special-number and with the</p><p style="text-align: justify;">date of the comparison, and shall give a certificate in respect of it in the prescribed form, certifying that on the said date the apparatus was compared with the standard Test Apparatus and was found to agree with it within the prescribed limits, and specifying any corrections to be made in the results of tests carried out with the apparatus.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) A certificate granted under this section shall be valid for such period as may be prescribed.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(4) A certificate granted under this section shall, during the period for which it is valid, be proof, until the contrary is proved, of any matter stated therein.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(5) The officer shall keep a register in the prescribed form of all certificates granted by him under this section.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Testing officers</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">17. The Government may authorise any officer by name or by virtue of office to test petroleum of which samples have been taken under this Act, or which may have been submitted to him for test by any person, and to grant certificates of the results of such tests.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Manner of test</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">18. All tests of petroleum made under this Act, shall be made with a test apparatus in respect of which there is a valid certificate under section 16, shall have due regard to any correction specified in that certificate, and shall be carried out in accordance with rules made under section 21.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Certificate of testing</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">19. (1) The testing officer after testing samples of petroleum shall make out a certificate in the prescribed form, stating whether the petroleum is 49[ class I] or 50[ Class II], and if the petroleum is 51[ class II], the flashing-point of the petroleum. (2) The testing officer shall furnish the person concerned, at his request, with a certified copy of the certificate, on payment of the prescribed fee, and such certified copy may be produced in any Court in proof of the contents of the original certificate.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) A certificate given under this section shall be admitted as evidence in any proceeding which may be taken under this Act in respect, or the petroleum from which the samples were taken, and shall until the contrary is proved, be conclusive proof that the petroleum is, 52[ class I] or 53[ class II] as the case may be, and, if the petroleum is 54[ class II], of its flashing point.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Right to require re-tests</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">20.(1) The owner of any petroleum, or his agent, who is dissatisfied with the result of the test of the petroleum may, within seven days from the date on which he received intimation of the result of the test, apply to the officer empowered under section 14 to have fresh samples of the petroleum taken and tested.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) On such application and on payment of the prescribed fee, fresh samples of the petroleum shall be taken in the presence of such owner or agent or person deputed by him, and shall be tested in the presence of such owner or agent or person deputed by him.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) If, on such re-test, it appears that the original test was erroneous, the testing officer shall cancel the original certificate granted under section 19, shall make out a fresh certificate, and shall furnish the owner of the petroleum, or his agent, with a certified copy thereof, free of charge.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Power to make rules regarding tests</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">21. The Government may make rules-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) for the specification, verification, correction and replacement of the Standard Test Apparatus;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) prescribing fees for the inspection of the Standard Test Apparatus;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c) regulating the procedure in comparing a test apparatus with the Standard Test Apparatus;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d) prescribing the form of certificate to be given in respect of a test apparatus so compared, and the period for which such certificates shall be valid;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(e) prescribing the form of the register of such certificates;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(f) prescribing fees for comparing a test apparatus with the Standard Test Apparatus;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(g) regulation the procedure of testing officers in carrying out tests of petroleum, providing for the averaging of results where several samples of the same petroleum are tested, and prescribing the variations from standard temperatures which may be allowed;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(h) prescribing the form of certificates of tests of petroleum and the fees which may be charged therefor;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(i) providing where the results of the testing of samples raise a doubt as to the uniformity of the quality of the petroleum in any lot under test, for the division of the lot into sub-lots, and for the selection and testing of samples of each sub-lot and for the averaging of results in accordance with the results of tests of those samples;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(j) prescribing fees for re-tests under section 20 and providing for their refund where the original test was erroneous; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(k) generally, regulating the procedure of all officers performing duties connected with the testing of petroleum and providing for any matter incidental to such testing.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Special rules for testing viscous or solid forms of petroleum</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">22. The Government may also make rules providing specially for the testing of any form of petroleum which is viscous or solid or contains sediment or thickening ingredients, and such rules may modify or supplement any of the provisions of this Chapter or of the rules made under section 21 in order to adapt them to the special needs of such tests.</p><p align="center">CHAPTER III</p><p align="center">PENALTIES AND PROCEDURE</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>General penalty for offences under this Act</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">23.(1) Whoever-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) in contravention of any of the provisions of Chapter I or of any of the rules made thereunder, imports, transports, 55[ stores, distributes] produces, 56[ refines, blends or reclaims by recycling] blends any petroleum, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) contravenes any rule made under section 4 or section 5, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c) being the holder of a licence issued under section 4 or a person for the time being placed by the holder of such licence in control or in charge of any place where petroleum is being imported 57[ , stored or distributed] or is under transport, contravenes any condition of such licence or suffers any condition of such licence to be contravened, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d) being for the time in control or in charge of any place where petroleum is being imported, 58[ stored,</p><p style="text-align: justify;">distributed] produced, 59[ refined, blended or reclaimed by recycling] or is under transport, refuses or neglects to show to any officer authorised under section 13 any receptacle, plant or appliance used in such place in connection with petroleum, or in any way obstructs or fails to render reasonable assistance to such officer during an inspection, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(e) being for the time being in control or in charge of any place where petroleum is being imported, transported 60[ stored, distributed], produced, 61[ refined, blended or reclaimed by recycling] refuses or neglects to show to any officer authorised under section 14 any petroleum in such place, or to give him such assistance as he may require for the inspection of such petroleum or refuses to allow him to take samples of the petroleum, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(f) being required, under section 27, to give information of an accident fails to give such information as so required by that section,</p><p style="text-align: justify;">shall be punishable 62[ with imprisonment for a term which may extend to three months, or with fine which may extend to five thousand Taka, or with both].</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) If any person, having been convicted of an offence punishable under sub-section (1), is again guilty of any offence punishable under that sub-section, he shall be punishable for every such subsequent offence with 63[ with imprisonment for a term which may extend to six months, or with fine which may extend to ten thousand Taka, or with both].</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Confiscation of petroleum and receptacles</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">24.(1) In any case in which an offence under clause (a) or clause (b) or clause (c) or sub-section (1) of section 23 has been committed, the convicting Magistrate may direct that?</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) the petroleum in respect of which the offence has been committed, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) where the offender is convicted of importing, transporting 64[ , storing or distributing] petroleum exceeding the quantity he is permitted to import, transport 65[ , store or distribute] as the case may be, the whole of the petroleum in respect of which the offence was committed,</p><p style="text-align: justify;">shall, together with the receptacles in which it is contained, be confiscated.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) This power may also be exercised by the 66[ High Court Division] in the exercise of its appellate or revisional powers.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Jurisdiction</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">25. Offences punishable under this Act shall be triable, by a Magistrate of the first class, or by a Magistrate of the second class who has been specially empowered by the Government in this behalf.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Power of entry and search</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">26.(1) The Government may, by notification in the official Gazette, authorise any officer by name or by virtue of office to enter and search any place where he has reason to believe that any petroleum is being imported, transported, 67[ stored, distributed],</p><p style="text-align: justify;">produced, 68[ refined, blended or reclaimed by recycling] otherwise than in accordance with the provisions of this Act and the rules made thereunder, and to seize, detain or remove any or all of the petroleum in respect of which in his opinion an offence under this Act has been committed.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The provisions of the Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898, relating to searches shall, so far as they are applicable, apply to searches by officers authorised under this section.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) The Government may make rules regulating the procedure of authorised officers in the exercise of their powers under this section subject, how ever, to the provisions of sub-section (2).</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Reports of accidents with petroleum</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">27. Where any accident by explosion or fire, which is attended with loss of human life or serious injury to person or property, occurs as the result of the ignition of petroleum or petroleum vapour, or occurs in or near any place where petroleum is kept and under circumstances making it likely that it was the result of such ignition, the person for the time being in charge of the petroleum shall forthwith give information to the nearest Magistrate or to the officer in charge of the nearest police station 69[ and to the Chief Inspector of Explosives in Bangladesh].</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Inquiries into serious accidents with petroleum</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">28. (1) The inquiry mentioned in section 176 of the Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898, shall 70[ * * *] be held in all cases where any person has been killed by an accident which the</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Magistrate has reason to believe was the result of the ignition of petroleum or petroleum vapour.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) Any Magistrate empowered to hold an inquest may also hold an inquiry under the said section into the cause of any accident which he has reason to believe was the result of the ignition of petroleum or petroleum vapour, if such accident was attended by serious injury to person or property, not-withstanding that no person was killed thereby.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) 71[ Omitted by the Adaptation of Central Acts and Ordinances Order, 1949.]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(4) The result of all inquires held in pursuance of this section 72[ * * *] shall be submitted as soon as may be to the Government, the Chief Inspector of Explosives in Bangladesh 73[ * * *].</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Report to be submitted to chief Inspector of explosives</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">74[ 28A. The officer authorised under sections 13, 14 and 26 shall furnish a copy of the report on the matter enquired into, or searched, by him in accordance with the provisions of these sections to the Chief Inspector of Explosives in Bangladesh.]</p><p align="center">CHAPTER IV</p><p align="center">SUPPLEMENTAL</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Provisions relating to rules</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">29.(1) In marking any rules under this Act, the Government may-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        provide for any matter ancillary to such rules for</p><p style="text-align: justify;">which in its opinion provision is necessary to protect the public from danger arising from the import, transport, 75[ storage, distribution] production, 76[ refining, blending or reclaiming by recycling] of petroleum, and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) make special provision for the special circumstances of any 77[ * * *] place.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) Every power to make rules conferred by this Act is subject to the condition of previous publication.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) All rules made under this Act shall be published in the official Gazette.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Power to apply Act to other substances</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">30.(1) The Government may, by notification in the official Gazette, apply any or all of the provisions of this Act, and of the rules made thereunder with such modifications as it may specify, to any dangerously inflammable substance, other than an explosive, and there upon the provisions so applied shall have effect as if such substance has been included in the definition of petroleum.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The Government may make rules providing specially for the testing of any substance to which any of the provisions of this Act have been applied by notification under sub-section (1) and such rules may supplement any of the provisions of chapter II in order to adapt them to the special needs of such tests.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Power to limit powers of local authorities over petroleum</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">31. Where any enactment confers powers upon any local authority in respect of the transport or storage of petroleum, the Government may, by notification in the official Gazette,-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) limit the operation of such enactment, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) restrict the exercise of the powers, in any manner it deems fit.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">[Repealed]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">32. [Repealed by sections 2 and Schedule of the Repealing Act, 1938 (Act No. 1 of 1938).]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">__________________________________________</p><p style="text-align: justify;">1
